Date:  Sat, 06 Jan 2018 19:32:47 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2016 R2 PANSTARRS (Dec.15,2017)
Object/Date:
Comet C/2016 R2 (PANSTARRS) @ Dec.15,2017 02:34 UT

Description:
Comet C/2016 R2 (PANSTARRS) photographed on December 15th 2017. This comet increased its activity suddenly in middle November and from then has deployed a very dynamic ionic tail. In this high resolution image taken through telescope IAC-80 from Teide Observatory can be seen multiple jets ejected from nucleus in all directions, as well as changing clouds of plasma emerging from coma and waving behind with the solar wind.

Tech data:
Telescope IAC-80 0.82m f/11.3 & camera Camelot (L:8×90s Bin1) from Teide Observatory, Canary Islands (Spain)
Paula Sola & José J. Chambó

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2016r2-panstarrs-20171215/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
(Valencia, Spain)

blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: facebook.com/JoseJChambo

Date:  Wed, 10 Jan 2018 22:45:37 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2016 R2 PANSTARRS (Jan.07,2018)
Object/Date:
C/2016 R2 (PANSTARRS) @ Jan 7,2018 02:42 UT

Description:
Comet C/2016 R2 (PANSTARRS) photographed on January 7th 2018. Still to four months of its perihelion shows a great activity in shape of a unusual ionic tail, intensely bluish because its composition of carbon monoxid, and waving in shreds at mercy of the solar wind. The bright star at down-left is Gamma Tauri, the star at the apex of the V-shaped Hyades star cluster in Taurus.

Tech data:
Planewave 20" CDK f/4,5 & FLI-PL11002M 2x(360sec) desde Mayhill, Nuevo México (EEUU) from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2016r2-panstarrs-20180107/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
(Valencia, Spain)

blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: facebook.com/JoseJChambo

From:  Damian Peach 
Subject:  Comet C/2016 R2 on Jan 7th in colour
Hi all,
With the help of colour data taken by Jose J. Chambo of the same field several hours earlier i was able to produce a colour image by using my B filter image (sent previously) with Jose's colour data. The result turned out rather nicely.
http://www.damianpeach.com/deepsky/c2016_r2_2018_01_07dpjjc.jpg

16"ASA + 20"CDK. BRGB. L=36min. RGB=5min.D. Peach & Jose J. Chambo.

Best Wishes
Damian

Subject:  Comet Panstarrs R2 - One night steady seeing.  1/17/18
Greetings all,

Had a nice clear night before a huge winter storm moves in tomorrow, and took a long look at this enigmatic object. Still hints of a green / teal coloration near the head, but a cobalt blue tail. Thanks for looking:

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/CometPanstarrsR2-011718.html

From: Chris Schur comets133@yahoo.com [Comet-Images]

Subject: [Comet-Images] Comet Panstarrs R2 - One night steady seeing. 1/17/18

Greetings all,

Had a nice clear night before a huge winter storm moves in tomorrow, and took a long look
at this enigmatic object. Still hints of a green / teal coloration near the head, but a
cobalt blue tail. Thanks for looking:

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/CometPanstarrsR2-011718.html

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Date:  Tue, 30 Jan 2018 00:20:44 +0000
From:  hiroc070717@yahoo.com
Subject:  C/2016 R2 under Moon Light January 27, 2018
Hi all,

I tried imaging of the comet under Moon Light. Ten Day moon was near, 7 degrees apart at the night.

https://www.flickr.com/photos/hiroc/25085395677 https://www.flickr.com/photos/hiroc/25085395677

The comet was reported to showing strong CO+ and N2+ emission, and I tried imaging with 425nm filter, Edmund #87-799. Band width is said to be 25nm, not so narrow bandpass filter.
https://www.edmundoptics.com/optics/optical-filters/bandpass-filters/425nm-cwl-50mm-dia.-hard-coated-od-4-25nm-bandpass-filter/ https://www.edmundoptics.com/optics/optical-filters/bandpass-filters/425nm-cwl-50mm-dia.-hard-coated-od-4-25nm-bandpass-filter/

Sky was blue under moon light due to Rayleigh scattering of reflected solar light as daytime, and it interfered the imaging with filter of band in blue range. I could not make long exposure then, up to 80 seconds, and I could not recognize the comet even on the stacked frame before enhancement. Story was different from imaging with hydrogen-alpha filter in full moon night.

Regards,
Hisayoshi Kato 
Date:  Tue, 30 Jan 2018 05:35:02 +0000
From:  hiroc070717@yahoo.com
Subject:  C/2016 R2 near Moon January 27, 2018
Hi all,

I tried imaging of the comet with 425nm filter.

https://www.flickr.com/photos/hiroc/25085395677 https://www.flickr.com/photos/hiroc/25085395677

The 425nm filter was not a strong tool on blue sky under moon light.

Regards,
Hisayoshi Kato

Date:  Mon, 29 Jan 2018 12:50:37 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  62P/Tsuchinshan (Dec.15,2017)
Object/Date:
Comet 62P/Tsuchinshan @ Dec.15,2017 05:55 UT

Description:
Comet 62P/Tsuchinshan photographed on December 15th 2017 through telescope IAC80 of Teide Observatory. This high resolution image shows a faint external coma with some 300.000 Km. diameter enveloping a sharp central condensation from wich emerges a short tail toward Northwest.

Tech data:
Telescope IAC-80 0.82m f/11.3 & camera Camelot (L:8×60s Bin1) from Teide Observatory, Canary Islands (Spain)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/62p-tsuchinshan-20171215/

Clear and dark skies.

Date:  Thu, 08 Feb 2018 18:22:59 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet Panstarrs R2 in a nebulous background - 2/7/18
HI all,

I went long and deep with the 10" f/3.9 last night on this comet, and also used a blue filter for the Luminance. Closest approach to M45 is around now, and the background has tons of outer nebulosity from this cluster to make processing interesting. The tail is fairly short now, but sports a nice fan shape and some included spiky rays. The comet is really quite faint!

On my first processing attempt, I tried to remove the stars from the stack by all the standard methods (Sigma, median, etc.) , and it was not going well. The tail is so faint that you have to really stretch the image to see it fully. But then the hordes of overlapping star streaks fill the tail. Because the comet is moving so slowly, sigma or median stacking is not really effective here. Heroic attempts with the cloning or patch tool made the comet look like tic-tac-toe. Oh my. I guess with a fast optical system you have to come to the realization that for really dim slow moving comets in rich star fields, the best way is the classic approach of stationary comet and trailed stars. ;)

Here is last nights shot:

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/CometPanstarrsR2-020718.html

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

C/2016 R2 (PANSTARRS) @ Feb 4,2018 02:01 UT

Description:
Comet C/2016 R2 (PANSTARRS) photographed on February 4th 2018 during its conjunction with the Pleiades open star cluster (Messier 45). The comet deploys a long blue tail inside our Solar System composed by carbon monoxide ionized because solar wind, whereas that blue nebulosity around star cluster are clouds of interstellar dust (visible for whole image) enlightened by brightest stars. The image is a mosaic composed by three tiles filling a field of 7 x 2 degrees.

Tech data:
Takahashi FSQ-106F f/5,0 & SBIG STL-11000M, from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2016r2-panstarrs-20180204/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
(Valencia, Spain)

blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: facebook.com/JoseJChambo

Date:  Thu, 15 Feb 2018 03:41:20 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet Panstarrs R2 on Sunday Night
HI all,

The comet continues to have a dim but impressive tail, with a rich blue coloration. It is near the zenith at the end of astronomical twilight, allowing us to get in about 2 hours before the comet moves behind the trees next to our house. Clouds from an oncoming winter storm took out the last 30 minutes of shooting, but I still got a good 90 minutes and RGB data too. Here is the results with the 10 inch f/3.9 and ST10xme CCD:

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/CometPanstarrsR2-021118.html

Clear Skies,

Chris Schur

Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

Date:  Mon, 26 Feb 2018 01:41:05 +0000
From:  hiroc070717@yahoo.com
Subject:  Re: Blue Comet C/2016 R2 on February 17, 2018
Hi Chris,

The comet is small and faint, though the tail is brilliant blue.

The blue is reported to be emission of monocarbonate ion.

"Stron CO+ and N2+ Emission in Comet C/2016 R" (Pan-STARRS)"
https://arxiv.org/abs/1801.01199

Monocarbonate ion, CO+ emits light around 425nm in wavelength.
Edmund optics #87-799 425nm bandpass filter was available.
https://www.edmundoptics.com/optics/optical-filters/bandpass-filters/425nm-cwl-50mm-dia.-hard-coated-od-4-25nm-bandpass-filter/

I tried imaging of the comet with the filter on February 4, 2018.
https://www.flickr.com/photos/hiroc/39193896125

The tail was visible on the frame, though the background was uneven.

Here is a color frame, taken on the same night.
https://www.flickr.com/photos/hiroc/25235794267

This color frame shows that the uneven background is Taurus Molecular Cloud.
The cloud contains reflected light from surrounding stars, and the light is continuum.
Continuum light of stars contains 425nm light, and Taurus Molecular Cloud is also visible on the frame, taken with 425nm filter.

I feel that enhanced color saturation may be helpful to see the blue tail.

Rigard, hiro

From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2016 R2 PANSTARRS (Mar.6,2018)
Comet C/2016 R2 (PANSTARRS) photographed on March 6, 2018 seems less active in spite of be still to two months of perihelion, although keeps its appearance with a small coma from which departs a blue narrow ionic tail that is opening in distance.

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2016r2-panstarrs-20180306/


Clear and dark skies.

José J. Chambó
(Valencia, Spain)

Date:  Mon, 19 Mar 2018 19:52:16 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2016 R2 PANSTARRS (Jan.10,2018)
Object/Date:
C/2016 R2 (PANSTARRS) @ Jan 10,2018 20:53 UT

Description:
Another wide field image of C/2016 R2 (PANSTARRS) taken from a serial obtained from Teide Observatory during comet maximum. In this case on January 10th 2018, the beautiful blue tail is noted better because not be superimposed on interstellar clouds which fill up the field. Draw attention the sidestep what does ionic tail do, at mercy of solar wind.

Tech data:
Lens Canon EF 400mm. f/2,8 & Camera Sony Alpha-7s (48 × 30 sec. at ISO-5000), from TAD, Teide Observatory, Tenerife, Canary Islands (Spain)

José J. Chambó Bris / Miquel Serra Ricart / Galactica Project (FECYT, IAC)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2016r2-panstarrs-20180110/



Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
(Valencia, Spain)

Date:  Mon, 30 Apr 2018 14:56:03 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2016 M1 PANSTARRS (Apr.24, 2018)
Object/Date:
C/2016 M1 (PANSTARRS) @ Apr 24,2018 10:36 UT

Description:
First image I took of the C/2016 M1 (PANSTARRS), this comet will reach its maximum brightness on next June when it could be observable visually through small telescopes or giant binoculars. In this image taken on April 24, 2018 can be seen a faint greenish coma wich has grown until a diameter of 6 arcminutes, al same time appears certain dust emission toward northwest (to up right).

Tech data:
Telescope Planewave 17" CDK f/4,5 & Camera FLI PL6303E (L=3x180sec bin1 + RGB=1x60sec bin2) from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2016m1-panstarrs-20180424/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
(Valencia, Spain)

Date:  Fri, 18 May 2018 21:37:47 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2016 M1 PANSTARRS (May.13, 2018)
Object/Date:
C/2016 M1 (PANSTARRS) @ May.13,2018 02:53 UT

Description:
Comet C/2016 M1 (PANSTARRS) continue increasing brightness and size, such as can be observed in this image on May 13th 2018. Its evolution is clear if we compare with my previous image taken three weeks ago, its greenish coma grew from 6 to 8 arcminutes of apparent diameter while its brightness has increased from magnitude 10.5 to 9.5.

Tech data:
Telescope GSO 8" f/3.8 & Camera Atik 383L+ (L:4x180s Bin1 + RGB:1x60s Bin2) from Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2016r2-panstarrs-20180513/

Clear and dark skies.

From:  denis buczynski 
Subject:  BAA Publication The Comet's Tale latest edtion
Thanks to the very hard work of our editor, Janice McClean, the latest issue of the Section's newsletter, issue 37, is available online here. This is a bumper edition of 59 pages with articles from nine different authors and many examples of the excellent work done by comet observers from around the world. I hope you enjoy reading it.If you have any comments or suggestions or would like to write an article for a future Comet's Tale please contact me.The full archive of Comet's Tale going back to issue 1 from 1994 November is available here and even older section publications going back to 1973 are here.

Date:  Sat, 23 Jun 2018 16:20:12 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet 66P/duToit (June 21, 2018)
66P/du Toit & NGC 253 @ Jun 21,2018 17:25 UT

Comet 66P/du Toit photographed on June 21th 2018 when was in conjunction with Sculptor Galaxy, also known as Silver Dollar Galaxy or NGC 253, a spiral with intense star formation to 12 million light-years from Earth. Meanwhile, the periodic comet 66P visiting us every 15 years is these days near our planet showing a intense green coma and observable from Southern Hemisphere through medium-size telescopes.

Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/4.4 & Camera FLI PL09000.
Mosaic of 2 tiles, 9 min. each. Non-composite stacking.
Remotely from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/66p-dutoit-20180621/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Date:  Sat, 07 Jul 2018 17:26:49 +0200
From:  Erik Bryssinck 
Subject:  RE: [Comet-Images] Re: image C/2017 S3 7/7/18
Hi Ron,

Thanks for watching !

This comet is not brightening anymore according the observations of this morning, i don’t have data for 6 july due cloudy weather. You can see on the Af(rho) vs julian date that this parameter is much lower in comparison with 7 july vs 5 july – 128 cm on 7/7 vs 273 cm on 5/7 . So less activity now… the magnitude was also lower this morning

Best regards,

Erik

Date:  Fri, 13 Jul 2018 17:30:54 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2016 M1 PANSTARRS (Jun.21,2018)
I'm sorry, a delayed image...

Object/Date:
C/2016 M1 (PANSTARRS) @ June 21,2018 17:05 UT

Description:
Comet C/2016 M1 (PANSTARRS) photographed on June 21, 2018 over a thousand stars background of Milky Way in Corona Australis constellation. With a brightness of magnitude 8.5 the comet is now at maximum approaching to Earth (1.3 A.U., about 500 times the distance to the Moon) and is observable through binoculars from dark places. In this image the comet shows a greenish coma with a diameter of 10 arcminutes and a tail of half degree lenght.

Tech data:
Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/4.4 & Camera FLI PL09000.
9 min. total exposure. Non-composite stacking.
Remotely from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2016m1-panstarrs-20180621/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia 

Date:  Fri, 13 Jul 2018 18:42:02 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2017 S3 PANSTARRS (Jul.5,2018)
Object/Date:
C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) @ July 5,2018 02:26 UT

Description:
Image of comet C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) taken during an outburst that happened at the beginning of July 2018, in wich its brightness increased from magnitude 12 to 9 meanwhile its coma expanded so from 2.5 to 5 arcminutes of appearent size (nearly from 150.000 to 300.000 Km. real diameter). The intense greenish tone of coma suggest that major part of emitted material is about C2 gas (diatomic carbon).

Tech data:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8 & Camera Atik 383L+.
14.5 min. total exposure. Non-composite stacking.
Locally from Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2017s3-panstarrs-20180705/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

On Saturday, July 14, 2018, 2:42:10 AM GMT+8, José J. Chambó jjchambo@hotmail.com [Comet-Images] wrote:

Object/Date:
C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) @ July 5,2018 02:26 UT

Description:
Image of comet C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) taken during an outburst that happened at the beginning of July 2018, in wich its brightness increased from magnitude 12 to 9 meanwhile its coma expanded so from 2.5 to 5 arcminutes of appearent size (nearly from 150.000 to 300.000 Km. real diameter). The intense greenish tone of coma suggest that major part of emitted material is about C2 gas (diatomic carbon).

Tech data:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8 & Camera Atik 383L+.
14.5 min. total exposure. Non-composite stacking.
Locally from Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2017s3-panstarrs-20180705/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Date:  Tue, 17 Jul 2018 15:20:21 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2017 S3 PANSTARRS (Jul.9,2018)
Object/Date:
C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) @ July 9,2018 02:42 UT

Description:
Comet C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) photographed on July 9th 2018, a week after its first outburst of activity has dropped from magnitude 9 to 10.5 with a coma which has reduced again its size from 5 to 3 arcseconds in appearent diameter. In the upper part of the image highlights "Tombaugh 5", a little-known open cluster of faint 12 magnitude stars.

Tech data:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8 & Camera Atik 383L+.
14.5 min. total exposure. Non-composite stacking.
Locally from Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2017s3-panstarrs-20180709/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

From:  Erik Bryssinck 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] image C/2017 S3 & spectrum
Hi Chris,

Thanks for watching.

the light pollution is indeed subtracted from the rough image, the spectrum you see is the netto spectrum of the comet only with here and there a very small amount of a rest of the light pollution. You would otherwise get a different graph :). The BASS software , i use for the processing, has the necessary tools for these operations.

hope this helps.

best regards
Erik

Van: "Comet-Images"
Aan: "Comet-Images"
Verzonden: Donderdag 19 juli 2018 21:39:10

Couldnt you take a spectrum of a nearby field and subtract to get the comet only?

Date:  Sat, 21 Jul 2018 19:09:09 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2017 S3 PANSTARRS (Jul.15,2018)
Object/Date:
C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) @ July 15,2018 02:29 UT

Description:
Image of comet C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) on July 15th 2018, photographed just when was happening a second outburst and increasing suddenly its brightness from magnitude 10.5 to 8. If we compares with the image I took on day 9th we will see its coma extended the size from 3' to 4', but mainly changed its appearance much more condensed and contrasted wich reveal recent gas emission still in expansion phase. On the other hand, begins to be appreciable the developing of a ionic tail toward northwest, although appears faint and short in this image.

Tech data:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8 & Camera Atik 383L+.
9 min. total exposure. Non-composite stacking.
Locally from Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2017s3-panstarrs-20180715/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Date:  Mon, 23 Jul 2018 15:37:22 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2017 S3 PANSTARRS (Jul.19,2018)
Object/Date:
C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) @ July 19,2018 02:42 UT

Description:
Comet C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) photographed on July 19th 2018, after a second outburst of activity, increased its brightness until magnitude 7 and expanding its greenish coma until a apparent diameter of 8', being observable through binoculars in the sky before dawn and developing a ionic tail which in this image is perceived with at least half degree lenght.

Tech data:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8 & Camera Atik 383L+.
11 min. total exposure. Non-composite stacking.
Locally from Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2017s3-panstarrs-20180719/


Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8 & Camera Atik
383L+.

Locally from Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

http://cometografia.es/2017s3-panstarrs-20180719/

Date:  Tue, 24 Jul 2018 20:32:09 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2017 S3 PANSTARRS (Jul.20,2018)


Object/Date:
C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) @ July 20,2018 10:17 UT

Description:
Comet C/2017 S3 (PANSTARRS) photographed on July 20th 218, after a pair of outbursts developed a ionic tail during some days, but this one weaken fast. In this image the tail had already started to vanish, although still is appreciable some structural detail in it.

Tech data:
Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/4.5 & Camera FLI PL11002M.
Mosaic of 2 tiles, 9 min. each. Non-composite stacking.
Remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2017s3-panstarrs-20180720/



Clear and dark skies.

Date:  Sun, 26 Aug 2018 00:13:53 -0700
From:  schmidtcamera250070@yahoo.com
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 21P August 22
Dear JFS. It takes a little longer to remove the individual stars from each image so carefully.
To my images, it should be noted that the CMOS camera is in blue-green
more sensitive than in red. For L I take a mix from the blue-green channel
with a weighting towards blue. Such a image shows much more the gas-rich coma and less the dust tail. I like it that much better. But as always - the color images are just pretty pictures. Regards Michael

Date:  Sat, 01 Sep 2018 14:22:02 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet 21P/Giacobini-Zinner (August 12,2018)
Object/Date:
21P/Giacobini-Zinner @ August 12,2018 02:45 UT

Description:
Comet 21P / Giacobini-Zinner photographed on August 12th 2018 grazing the Milky Way border in Cassiopeia more dense of stars (down). The comet has considerably increased its angular size showing a turquoise color with 9' wich wrapping nucleus. Its dust tail reaches 40' lenght inside within which can be seen a ionic jet more condensed.

Acquisition:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8 & Camera Atik 383L+.
12 min. total exposure.
>From Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/21p-giacobini-zinner-20180812/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Date:  Mon, 03 Sep 2018 22:08:42 +0000
From:  drygulch_99@yahoo.com
Subject:  Comet 21 P on 2018-09-02 @ 9:36:20 UT to 10:34:29 UT
Here is our stacked image, animation and inverted animation of Comet 21P. This was done with a cheap astrovideo camera AVS DSO 1 captured to a mini DVR. Telescope Vixen 130 mm,f/5 Reflector telescope. Each animation frame is a frame integration then a video stack of about 40 second exposure. Seeing was about 6/7 ,Transparency about 7/8 with a 59% illuminated Moon. This is about the best our junk can do!
https://vimeo.com/287988209 https://vimeo.com/287988209 

Date:  Tue, 04 Sep 2018 09:03:11 -0500
From:  Bob King 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Comet 21P/ GZ from Arizona
And while you've dealt with that, we've been covered in smoke for weeks.
Finally, we got a clear night Sunday. The sky was incredible. Got to see
our friend the comet in binocs and through the 15-inch. Also viewed the
mysterious 64P/Swift-Gehrels post-outburst. One of the most diffuse objects
I've seen in a while.

Bob

Date:  Tue, 04 Sep 2018 20:03:02 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  21P/Giacobini-Zinner (August 20, 2018) and internal structure
Object/Date:
Comet 21P/Giacobini-Zinner @ August 20,2018 03:06 UT

Description:
Comet 21P/Giacobini-Zinner some days before its maximum approaching. In this full shot of the comet on August 20th 2018 was taken at same time through of TAR2 Telescope in Teide Observatory and my habitual equipment from Hoya Redonda. Besides of the image showing comet appearance, objective of shots were to register internal coma structures using gradient filters. The second version of this image adds graphical wich shows internal coma enlarged and filtered (inverted monochrome) revealing the presence of four jets emerging from nucleus.

Acquisition details:
Centurion 18" CRC f/2.8, SBIG STL-11000M (L) & GSO 8" N f/3.8, Atik 383L+ (RGB).
112 min. total exposure.
>From Teide Observatory, Canary Islands and Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain).

Credits:
José J. Chambó Bris / Miquel Serra-Ricart / Javier Licandro / TAR2 (Teide Observatory, IAC)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/21p-giacobini-zinner-20180820/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Object/Date:
Comet 21P/Giacobini-Zinner @ August 20,2018 03:06
UT

Description:
Comet 21P/Giacobini-Zinner some days before its maximum
approaching. In this full shot of the comet on August 20th
2018 was taken at same time through of TAR2 Telescope in
Teide Observatory and my habitual equipment from Hoya
Redonda. Besides of the image
showing comet appearance, objective of shots were to
register internal coma structures using gradient filters.
The second version of this image adds graphical wich shows
internal coma enlarged and filtered (inverted monochrome)
revealing the presence of four
jets emerging from nucleus.

Acquisition details:
Centurion 18" CRC f/2.8, SBIG STL-11000M (L) &
GSO 8" N f/3.8, Atik 383L+ (RGB).
112 min. total exposure.
From Teide Observatory, Canary Islands and Hoya
Redonda, Valencia (Spain).

José J. Chambó Bris / Miquel Serra-Ricart / Javier
Licandro / TAR2 (Teide Observatory, IAC)

Date:  Wed, 12 Sep 2018 09:43:54 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet 21P/Giacobini-Zinner at perihelion
Object/Date:
21P/Giacobini-Zinner @ 2018 September 10, 10:30 UT

Description:
Comet 21P/Giacobini-Zinner imaged on September 10th 2018, just on its perihelion day at minimum distance to Sun. Moreover almost coinciding with its maximum approaching to Earth, all this do the present apparition of periodical comet as the most favorable in decades. Located into constellation Auriga in the middle of the Milky Way on a full starfield and casually passing between the large open clusters M 36 at right and M 37 at left, also some reddish interstellar dust clouds can be detected mixing between stars.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Takahashi FSQ-106 f/5.0 & Camera SBIG STL-11000M.
Mosaic of 2 tiles, 9 min. each.
Remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/21p-giacobini-zinner-20180910/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

.

Date:  Tue, 25 Sep 2018 16:22:40 +0000
From:  schmidtcamera250070@yahoo.com
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 21P and NGC 2174/IC443
Hi Juanjo

I want to answer the eternal question about the workflow as follows.
As always you have to remove the stars from the frames. There are many good and bad ways.
The tool in Photoshop is not very useful. The combination of Astro Art and Fitswork is currently my favorite. Astro Art has a star removal tool under cosmetics. With that disappear more than 90 percent of the stars. Then I go into Fitswork and take down star radius. Then almost all stars are gone. At most you have to stamp.

As it looks like the single image taken on sep 18 UT 2.00 with 8"/2,8 and CCD.
Exposure time was 210sec.

http://spaceweathergallery.com/full_image.php?image_name=michael-jAcger-21P20180918ut200sec210_1537892231.jpg http://spaceweathergallery.com/full_image.php?image_name=michael-jAcger-21P20180918ut200sec210_1537892231.jpg

I am currently working on this exciting image.
Especially on this day the comet has shown a clearly visible ion tail.
I have 25 images to edit here. Only remove the stars takes more than 2-3 hours.
But then you can process the frames via median combine etc. well.
So the secret is as carefully as possible remove the stars.
The rest is normal workflow.
Regards Michael

I used Canon 6Da with 200 mm L II lens . Right now I processed single shot 120 second but still waiting for stack and processing 30 minutes taken with 200 mm and 30 minutes short exposures with 130 mm APO .

Hi all,
Been some time since my last comet image - but with 46P brightening i decided to image this one. Makes a nice break after months of planetary work!
http://www.damianpeach.com/deepsky/46p_2018_11_08dp.jpg
A faint tail is seen in this image - hopefully a sign of things to come!

20" F/3.6 ASA. FLI CCD. LRGB. 45/5/5/5min.
Best Wishes
Damian

Date:  Wed, 14 Nov 2018 23:38:50 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2018 V1 (Machholz-Fujikawa-Iwamoto) @ November 11
Object/Date:
C/2018 V1 (Machholz-Fujikawa-Iwamoto) @ November 11,2018 12:05 UT

Description:
New comet C/2018 V1 (Machholz-Fujikawa-Iwamoto) discovered on November 7h 2018 visually by Don Machholz (USA) and photographically by Shigehisa Fujikawa y Masayuki Iwamoto (Japan). In this image taken only four days after its discovery the comet has magnitude 9 at low altitude above horizon, and shows a greenish coma with 5' angular size from which departs a narrow and fain ionic tail towards northeast.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/4.5 & Camera FLI PL11002M.
7 min. total exposure.
Remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2018v1-machholz-fujikawa-iwamoto-20181111/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Date:  Tue, 20 Nov 2018 03:39:34 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Last chance for C/2018 V1 from Arizona
Hi all,
Its been like 3 weeks of solid clouds here in Arizona, then it finally cleared this week only to reveal that the sky was smoked out by all the California wild fires.  This morning was clear, and the smoke was a bit less so I set up my portable set up and tried to find it.  Even though the goto mount put me right on it, it took 10 minutes for me to be certain I was seeing it in a low power ocular.  it was REALLY faint and dimmed by the horizon murk near Venus.  A 15 minute set in poor seeing is what I got, and the color is stunning!  The moon is here now, and the comet is plunging into the sunrise.  Glad I got this one!
http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/Comet2018V1-111918.html

Schurs Astrophotography

Date:  Fri, 23 Nov 2018 23:31:41 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet 46P/Wirtanen (Nov.12,2018)
Object/Date:
46P/Wirtanen @ November 12,2018 21:28 UT

Description:
Comet 46P/Wirtanen in its thirteenth apparition, located on constellation Fornax and shining at magnitude 7 was photographed in this wide field image taken through a photo-lens from Namibian austral dark skies. Its turquoise coma reaches 45 arcminutes, larger than full moon, and will be growing in size and brightness until its maximum approach to Earth on December. In the image can be intuit a short ionic tail toward norteast.

Acquisition details:
Lens Canon 200mm. f/1.8, camera SBIG STT-8300.
84 min. total exposure.
>From Hakos Astrofarm (Namibia).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/46p-wirtanen-20181112/

Credits:
José J. Chambó Bris / Miquel Serra-Ricart / Galactica Project (FECYT, IAC)

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Date:  Sun, 25 Nov 2018 09:31:01 -0600
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 46p on Nov 25th
There is a very faint gas tail in the 10:30 clock position in the photo in question; at this time there is no other "bright tail", which would be a dust tail and not hidden by the large coma. Many have commented on the sudden demise of the prominent gas tail that had developed in past weeks and only a very slim and faint portion of that is now visible as can be seen in the photo.

Dr. Clay

Date:  Sun, 25 Nov 2018 16:27:46 +0000
From:  Martin Mobberley 
Subject:  Re: 46p on Nov 25th
Thanks for the kind comments!
The elongation is increasing and will be ~ 160 degrees around Dec 19th,
so viewing perspective will shrink the tail (it will be 'behind' the
Earth). Having said that, it's 1.08 AU from the Sun and not a big comet
either. Plus, the tail was not dramatic on the return before last, see
my very contrasty shot with a C14 from 2008 Feb 6.

http://www.theastronomer.org/comets/2008/46p_20080206_mpm.jpg

Regards,
Martin

Date:  Tue, 27 Nov 2018 09:18:44 +1100
From:  mmatti@westnet.com.au
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 46p on Nov 25th
Hi Folks,

The comet’s phase angle decreases to 18 degrees at closest approach, so pretty slim chance of seeing much of a tail then. (maybe 1-2 degrees)
Phase angle at the moment is 45 degrees, reasonably favourable for a tail > 2 degrees, yet we are not seeing much ion tail activity.
What we need is solar activity to drive the ion tail, but the Sun has been so quiet lately!

chees,
Michael Mattiazzo

From: mailto:Comet-Images@yahoogroups.com
Sent: Monday, November 26, 2018 2:25 AM
To: Comet-Images
Subject: Re: [Comet-Images] 46p on Nov 25th

I'm not an expert by any means so I'm throwing this out for discussion.... What little bit of ion tail we can see from this geometry should be "absorbed" into the coma as 46P reaches perihelion and the Sun-Earth-Comet alignment.
Tom

Date:  Sat, 01 Dec 2018 03:16:20 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet 46P/Wirtanen with the Meade "Cometracker"  11/29/18
Hi all,
For us in central Arizona, the comet has finally cleared the trees and the sky cleared for an evening.  Here is a 55 minute exposure set with the 33 year old Meade 622, a schmidt newtonian of six inches aperture made specifically for both viewing AND imaging comets.  Ive since modified it to be an astrograph by installing a solid focuser, and shortening the tube to increase backfocus.  Also I now use a Baader MPCC corrector and the combination of both correctors yields a sharp field at f/3.6.  Thanks for looking - its been a long wait for the sky to clear!
http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/Wirtanen112918.html

From: mailto:Comet-Images@yahoogroups.com
Sent: Saturday, December 01, 2018 4:16 AM
To: Comet Group
Subject: [Comet-Images] Comet 46P/Wirtanen with the Meade "Cometracker"
11/29/18

Hi all,

For us in central Arizona, the comet has finally cleared the trees and the
sky cleared for an evening. Here is a 55 minute exposure set with the 33
year old Meade 622, a schmidt newtonian of six inches aperture made
specifically for both viewing AND imaging comets. Ive since modified it to
be an astrograph by installing a solid focuser, and shortening the tube to
increase backfocus. Also I now use a Baader MPCC corrector and the
combination of both correctors yields a sharp field at f/3.6. Thanks for
looking - its been a long wait for the sky to clear!

http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/Wirtanen112918.html

Date:  Sat, 01 Dec 2018 15:04:27 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Comet 46P/Wirtanen with the Meade "Cometracker" 11/29/18
Thanks Rolando!  I cant wait to get this one in the 10 inch and CCD....
Clear Skies, Chris Schur Schur's Web Portal: http://www.schursastrophotography.com

On Saturday, December 1, 2018, 12:02:45 AM MST, 'rolando ligustri' rolando.ligustri@alice.it [Comet-Images] wrote:

bella!   From: mailto:Comet-Images@yahoogroups.comSent: Saturday, December 01, 2018 4:16 AMTo: Comet Group Subject: [Comet-Images] Comet 46P/Wirtanen with the Meade"Cometracker" 11/29/18

Hi all, For us in central Arizona, the comet has finally cleared the trees and thesky cleared for an evening.  Here is a 55 minute exposure set with the 33year old Meade 622, a schmidt newtonian of six inches aperture made specificallyfor both viewing AND imaging comets.  Ive since modified it to be anastrograph by installing a solid focuser, and shortening the tube to increasebackfocus.  Also I now use a Baader MPCC corrector and the combination ofboth correctors yields a sharp field at f/3.6.  Thanks for looking - itsbeen a long wait for the sky to clear! http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/Wirtanen112918.html
 Schurs Astrophotography

From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet Wirtanen  12/3/18
HI all,
Reporting from the great cloud state here in Arizona!  We had one night to get in some frames of this superb comet, I was able to get 90 mins of data.  The comet was so huge in my 10 inch in such a long exposure that it spilled off the edges of the frame.  Oh well, next (rare) clear night Ill back off to the Zeiss 80mm APO.
http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/Wirtanen120318.html

Date:  Tue, 11 Dec 2018 19:03:21 +0000
From:  D F 
Subject:  Re: 46P to day 8 AM EST
Nice shot but what's the satellite?
I'm guessing the field of view is of the order of 1 degree?And that the comet is at fairly high altitude?So a satellite near the Earth is going to be moving at roughly 7km/sec?All exposures were 60 seconds and assuming it's only on one of them that's 420km.If track is 0.25degress which equates to approx 100,000km by my calculations?
I've been taking lots of 30 second exposures with 200-300mm telephoto lenses and several times a year I get short tracks like this. I even tracked one in realtime across the sky for hours!Can't believe there are such bright satellites so far out?And I dare not suggest they are near Earth asteroids!
Others must have seen/photographed/explained these?
David MooreDublin
Date:  Tue, 11 Dec 2018 20:39:56 +0000
From:  roman.kulesza@hotmail.com
Subject:  Re: 46P to day 8 AM EST
Hi David , thank you so much .
Thanks for asking but no idea what satellite is it , sorry ;(
Right now I am 'Big" grandpa and just found some time for processing .
My exposures Start Time - 12:12:04 and End Time - 12:16:41 in Australia
8:12:04 am - 8 :16:41 am EST North America
FOV is 1.63 X 1.23 deg
I used T-68 0.28 m at f/2,2 = 620 mm
This time no PixInsight , I stretched classic way in curves and median filter for noise apply so comet is huge :)

Date:  Mon, 17 Dec 2018 11:21:33 +1100
From:  mmatti@westnet.com.au
Subject:  Comet Wirtanen meets the Pleiades
Hi Folks,

I’ve uploaded a photo to spaceweather.

Comet 46P Wirtanen is seen here a few degrees east of the Pleiades star cluster in Taurus.
It is now closest to the Earth, at 30 lunar distances, and sports a coma about 1.2 degrees wide.
In linear terms this equates to 270,000kms. For comparison, the Earth-Moon distance is 390,000 kms.
Photo details: 2018 Dec 16 at 12:20UT. Canon 60Da + Sigma 200mm lens. 4 min. FOV 7x5 deg. North below.
The comet is now fighting moonlight and is harder to see naked eye.
My last visual obs was mag 4.1 on dec 14.
cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo

http://spaceweathergallery.com/indiv_upload.php?upload_id=150189

Date:  Sat, 22 Dec 2018 20:45:16 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet 46P/Wirtanen (Dec.10,2018)
Object/Date:
46P/Wirtanen @ December 10,2018 06:16 UT

Description:
Comet 46P/Wirtanen shows in this wide field image taken on December 10th 2018 a huge coma with 1.5 degrees of angular size, three times the size of Moon seen from Earth. With a global integrated brightness at least in magnitude 4, as reference the brightest star to right is 94 Ceti with magnitude 5. The inner coma contrasts exhibing a whitish color, also the faint tail toward northeast (to down-left). The field appears scattered with tiny galaxies, some visible through comet atmosphere.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Takahashi FSQ-106ED f/5.0.
Camera SBIG STL-11000M.
15 min. total exposure.
Remotely from Mayhill, New Mexico (USA).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/46p-wirtanen-20181210/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

.

On Monday, December 24, 2018, 7:13:43 AM MST, 'Chris Cook' chris@cookphoto.com [Comet-Images] wrote:

The sky was clear yesterday evening so I was able to capture the Christmas Comet (46P/Wirtanen) and Capella in the same FOV. I used a Canon 6D DSLR attached to an Astro-Physics 130EDT. The total exposure consists of ten 30 seconds exposures at ISO1250. Even with the bright full Moon nearby, the comet was still visible in 7x50 binoculars. A beautiful pairing.

http://www.abmedia.com/astro/current/46P-Capella-130EDT.html

Chris

Date:  Tue, 25 Dec 2018 11:24:01 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet 46P/Wirtanen (Dec.10,2018)
Object/Date:
46P/Wirtanen @ 10-December-2018 23:15 UT

Description:
Nearly at zenith, comet 46P Wirtanen can be seen catched between vanes of spider which holds the camera situated on
focus of Telescope TAR1 in Teide Observatory, meanwhile is photographed. This panorama includes the Pleiades star
cluster near center of image, and a little beyond the red trace of California Nebula. At down, Hyades open star
cluster, including the bright star Aldebaran, shape central part of constellation Taurus.

Acquisition details:
Lens Samyang 16 mm. f/2.0.
Camera Canon EOS 100D.
90 sec. exposure at ISO 3200 (one shot).
>From Teide Observatory, Canary Islands (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/46p-wirtanen-atrapando-20181210/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Before the family celebration, a tiny observation window opened at the end of the dusk. It was very clear, the comet was immediately visible to the naked eye as a moon-sized spot in the sky with 4mag.

field of bw image is 11x9° it was processed with Larson Sekanina.
LRGB L-4x270 RGB 300/300/300 Zeiss Milvus 135/3.4 and Moravian G3-16200

Date:  Mon, 31 Dec 2018 02:17:00 +0000
From:  Chris Schur 
Subject:  Comet Wirtanen - Fits in the 10 inch again!  12/29/18
Hi all,
One advantage of a receding comet Wirtanen is that it it smaller in angular size and moving a bit slower.  Perfect fit for my 10 inch astrograph.  I was happy to get in one more night of shooting on comets before a huge snow storm arrives tomorrow.  We have here a nice variety of colored stars in the background, and the sky stayed steady and transparent during the hour of exposure.  Hope you like it.
http://www.schursastrophotography.com/newcomets/CometWirtanen122918.html
